> You are my helper and my deliverer!
> O my God, do not delay!

### Psalm 41

For the music director; a psalm of David.

> <a name="19:41:1">41:1</a> How happy is the one who treats the poor properly!
> When trouble comes, the Lord delivers him.
> <a name="19:41:2">41:2</a> May the Lord protect him and save his life!
> May he be blessed in the land!
> Do not turn him over to his enemies!
> <a name="19:41:3">41:3</a> The Lord supports him on his sickbed;
> you completely heal him from his illness.
> <a name="19:41:4">41:4</a> As for me, I said:
> “O Lord, have mercy on me!
> Heal me, for I have sinned against you!
> <a name="19:41:5">41:5</a> My enemies ask this cruel question about me,
> ‘When will he finally die and be forgotten?’
> <a name="19:41:6">41:6</a> When someone comes to visit, he pretends to be friendly;
> he thinks of ways to defame me,
> and when he leaves he slanders me.
> <a name="19:41:7">41:7</a> All who hate me whisper insults about me to one another;
> they plan ways to harm me.
> <a name="19:41:8">41:8</a> They say,
> ‘An awful disease overwhelms him,
> and now that he is bed-ridden he will never recover.’
> <a name="19:41:9">41:9</a> Even my close friend whom I trusted,
> he who shared meals with me, has turned against me.
> <a name="19:41:10">41:10</a> As for you, O Lord, have mercy on me and raise me up,
> so I can pay them back!”
> <a name="19:41:11">41:11</a> By this I know that you are pleased with me,
> for my enemy does not triumph over me.
> <a name="19:41:12">41:12</a> As for me, you uphold me because of my integrity;
> you allow me permanent access to your presence.
> <a name="19:41:13">41:13</a> The Lord God of Israel deserves praise
> in the future and forevermore!
> We agree! We agree!

## Book 2 (42–72)

### Psalm 42

For the music director; a well-written song by the Korahites.

> <a name="19:42:1">42:1</a> As a deer longs for streams of water,
> so I long for you, O God!
> <a name="19:42:2">42:2</a> I thirst for God,
> for the living God.
> I say, “When will I be able to go and appear in God’s presence?”
> <a name="19:42:3">42:3</a> I cannot eat, I weep day and night;
> all day long they say to me, “Where is your God?”
> <a name="19:42:4">42:4</a> I will remember and weep!
> For I was once walking along with the great throng to the temple of God,
> shouting and giving thanks along with the crowd as we celebrated the holy festival.
> <a name="19:42:5">42:5</a> Why are you depressed, O my soul?
> Why are you upset?
> Wait for God!
> For I will again give thanks
> to my God for his saving intervention.
> <a name="19:42:6">42:6</a> I am depressed,
> so I will pray to you while I am trapped here in the region of the upper Jordan,
> from Hermon, from Mount Mizar.
> <a name="19:42:7">42:7</a> One deep stream calls out to another at the sound of your waterfalls;
> all your billows and waves overwhelm me.
> <a name="19:42:8">42:8</a> By day the Lord decrees his loyal love,
> and by night he gives me a song,
> a prayer to the living God.
> <a name="19:42:9">42:9</a> I will pray to God, my high ridge:
> “Why do you ignore me?
> Why must I walk around mourning
> because my enemies oppress me?”
> <a name="19:42:10">42:10</a> My enemies’ taunts cut into me to the bone,
> as they say to me all day long, “Where is your God?”
> <a name="19:42:11">42:11</a> Why are you depressed, O my soul?
> Why are you upset?
> Wait for God!
> For I will again give thanks
> to my God for his saving intervention.

### Psalm 43

> <a name="19:43:1">43:1</a> Vindicate me, O God!
> Fight for me against an ungodly nation!
> Deliver me from deceitful and evil men!
> <a name="19:43:2">43:2</a> For you are the God who shelters me.
> Why do you reject me?
> Why must I walk around mourning
> because my enemies oppress me?
> <a name="19:43:3">43:3</a> Reveal your light and your faithfulness!
> They will lead me,
> they will escort me back to your holy hill,
> and to the place where you live.
> <a name="19:43:4">43:4</a> Then I will go to the altar of God,
> to the God who gives me ecstatic joy,
> so that I express my thanks to you, O God, my God, with a harp.
> <a name="19:43:5">43:5</a> Why are you depressed, O my soul?
> Why are you upset?
> Wait for God!
> For I will again give thanks
> to my God for his saving intervention.

### Psalm 44

For the music director; by the Korahites, a well-written song.

> <a name="19:44:1">44:1</a> O God, we have clearly heard;
> our ancestors have told us
> what you did in their days,
> in ancient times.
> <a name="19:44:2">44:2</a> You, by your power, defeated nations and settled our fathers on their land;
> you crushed the people living there and enabled our ancestors to occupy it.
> <a name="19:44:3">44:3</a> For they did not conquer the land by their swords,
> and they did not prevail by their strength,
> but rather by your power, strength and good favor,
> for you were partial to them.
> <a name="19:44:4">44:4</a> You are my king, O God!
> Decree Jacob’s deliverance!
> <a name="19:44:5">44:5</a> By your power we will drive back our enemies;
> by your strength we will trample down our foes!
> <a name="19:44:6">44:6</a> For I do not trust in my bow,
> and I do not prevail by my sword.
> <a name="19:44:7">44:7</a> For you deliver us from our enemies;
> you humiliate those who hate us.
> <a name="19:44:8">44:8</a> In God I boast all day long,
> and we will continually give thanks to your name. (Selah)
> <a name="19:44:9">44:9</a> But you rejected and embarrassed us!
> You did not go into battle with our armies.
> <a name="19:44:10">44:10</a> You made us retreat from the enemy.
> Those who hate us take whatever they want from us.
> <a name="19:44:11">44:11</a> You handed us over like sheep to be eaten;
> you scattered us among the nations.
> <a name="19:44:12">44:12</a> You sold your people for a pittance;
> you did not ask a high price for them.
> <a name="19:44:13">44:13</a> You made us an object of disdain to our neighbors;
> those who live on our borders taunt and insult us.
> <a name="19:44:14">44:14</a> You made us an object of ridicule among the nations;
> foreigners treat us with contempt.
> <a name="19:44:15">44:15</a> All day long I feel humiliated
> and am overwhelmed with shame,
> <a name="19:44:16">44:16</a> before the vindictive enemy
> who ridicules and insults me.
> <a name="19:44:17">44:17</a> All this has happened to us, even though we have not rejected you
> or violated your covenant with us.
> <a name="19:44:18">44:18</a> We have not been unfaithful,
> nor have we disobeyed your commands.
> <a name="19:44:19">44:19</a> Yet you have battered us, leaving us a heap of ruins overrun by wild dogs;
> you have covered us with darkness.
> <a name="19:44:20">44:20</a> If we had rejected our God,
> and spread out our hands in prayer to another god,
> <a name="19:44:21">44:21</a> would not God discover it,
> for he knows one’s thoughts?
> <a name="19:44:22">44:22</a> Yet because of you we are killed all day long;
> we are treated like sheep at the slaughtering block.
> <a name="19:44:23">44:23</a> Rouse yourself! Why do you sleep, O sovereign Master?
> Wake up! Do not reject us forever!
> <a name="19:44:24">44:24</a> Why do you look the other way,
> and ignore the way we are oppressed and mistreated?
> <a name="19:44:25">44:25</a> For we lie in the dirt,
> with our bellies pressed to the ground.
> <a name="19:44:26">44:26</a> Rise up and help us!
> Rescue us because of your loyal love!

### Psalm 45

For the music director; according to the tune of “Lilies;” by the Korahites, a well-written poem, a love song.

> <a name="19:45:1">45:1</a> My heart is stirred by a beautiful song.
> I say, “I have composed this special song for the king;
> my tongue is as skilled as the stylus of an experienced scribe.”
> <a name="19:45:2">45:2</a> You are the most handsome of all men!
> You speak in an impressive and fitting manner!
> For this reason God grants you continual blessings.
> <a name="19:45:3">45:3</a> Strap your sword to your thigh, O warrior!
> Appear in your majestic splendor!
> <a name="19:45:4">45:4</a> Appear in your majesty and be victorious!
> Ride forth for the sake of what is right,
> on behalf of justice!
> Then your right hand will accomplish mighty acts!
> <a name="19:45:5">45:5</a> Your arrows are sharp
> and penetrate the hearts of the king’s enemies.
> Nations fall at your feet.
> <a name="19:45:6">45:6</a> Your throne, O God, is permanent.
> The scepter of your kingdom is a scepter of justice.
> <a name="19:45:7">45:7</a> You love justice and hate evil.
> For this reason God, your God has anointed you
> with the oil of joy, elevating you above your companions.
> <a name="19:45:8">45:8</a> All your garments are perfumed with myrrh, aloes, and cassia.
> From the luxurious palaces comes the music of stringed instruments that makes you happy.
> <a name="19:45:9">45:9</a> Princesses are among your honored guests,
> your bride stands at your right hand, wearing jewelry made with gold from Ophir.
> <a name="19:45:10">45:10</a> Listen, O princess!
> Observe and pay attention!
> Forget your homeland and your family!
> <a name="19:45:11">45:11</a> Then the king will be attracted by your beauty.
> After all, he is your master! Submit to him!
> <a name="19:45:12">45:12</a> Rich people from Tyre
> will seek your favor by bringing a gift.
> <a name="19:45:13">45:13</a> The princess looks absolutely magnificent,
> decked out in pearls and clothed in a brocade trimmed with gold.
> <a name="19:45:14">45:14</a> In embroidered robes she is escorted to the king.
> Her attendants, the maidens of honor who follow her,
> are led before you.
> <a name="19:45:15">45:15</a> They are bubbling with joy as they walk in procession
> and enter the royal palace.
> <a name="19:45:16">45:16</a> Your sons will carry on the dynasty of your ancestors;
> you will make them princes throughout the land.
> <a name="19:45:17">45:17</a> I will proclaim your greatness through the coming years,
> then the nations will praise you forever.

### Psalm 46

For the music director; by the Korahites; according to the alamoth style; a song.

> <a name="19:46:1">46:1</a> God is our secure shelter;
> he is truly our helper in times of trouble.
> <a name="19:46:2">46:2</a> For this reason we do not fear when the earth shakes,
> and the mountains tumble into the depths of the sea,
> <a name="19:46:3">46:3</a> when its waves crash and foam,
> and the mountains shake before the surging sea. (Selah)
> <a name="19:46:4">46:4</a> The irrigation canals flowing from the river bring joy to the city of God,
> the special, holy dwelling place of the Sovereign One.
> <a name="19:46:5">46:5</a> God lives within it, it cannot be upended.
> God rescues it at the break of dawn.
> <a name="19:46:6">46:6</a> Nations make a commotion, kingdoms are upended.
> God gives a battle cry, the earth dissolves.
> <a name="19:46:7">46:7</a> The Lord, the invincible Warrior, is on our side!
> The God of Jacob is our protector! (Selah)
> <a name="19:46:8">46:8</a> Come! Witness the exploits of the Lord,
> who brings devastation to the earth!
> <a name="19:46:9">46:9</a> He brings an end to wars throughout the earth;
> he shatters the bow and breaks the spear;
> he burns the shields.
> <a name="19:46:10">46:10</a> He says, “Stop your striving and recognize that I am God!
> I will be exalted over the nations! I will be exalted over the earth!”
> <a name="19:46:11">46:11</a> The Lord, the invincible Warrior is on our side!
> The God of Jacob is our protector! (Selah)

### Psalm 47

For the music director; by the Korahites; a psalm.

> <a name="19:47:1">47:1</a> All you nations, clap your hands!
> Shout out to God in celebration!
> <a name="19:47:2">47:2</a> For the sovereign Lord is awe-inspiring;
> he is the great king who rules the whole earth!
> <a name="19:47:3">47:3</a> He subdued nations beneath us
> and countries under our feet.
> <a name="19:47:4">47:4</a> He picked out for us a special land
> to be a source of pride for Jacob, whom he loves. (Selah)
> <a name="19:47:5">47:5</a> God has ascended his throne amid loud shouts;
> the Lord has ascended his throne amid the blaring of ram’s horns.
> <a name="19:47:6">47:6</a> Sing to God! Sing!
> Sing to our king! Sing!
> <a name="19:47:7">47:7</a> For God is king of the whole earth!
> Sing a well-written song!
> <a name="19:47:8">47:8</a> God reigns over the nations!
> God sits on his holy throne!
> <a name="19:47:9">47:9</a> The nobles of the nations assemble,
> along with the people of the God of Abraham,
> for God has authority over the rulers of the earth.
> He is highly exalted!

### Psalm 48

A song, a psalm by the Korahites.

> <a name="19:48:1">48:1</a> The Lord is great and certainly worthy of praise
> in the city of our God, his holy hill.
> <a name="19:48:2">48:2</a> It is lofty and pleasing to look at,
> a source of joy to the whole earth.
> Mount Zion resembles the peaks of Zaphon;
> it is the city of the great king.
> <a name="19:48:3">48:3</a> God is in its fortresses;
> he reveals himself as its defender.
> <a name="19:48:4">48:4</a> For look, the kings assemble;
> they advance together.
> <a name="19:48:5">48:5</a> As soon as they see, they are shocked;
> they are terrified, they quickly retreat.
> <a name="19:48:6">48:6</a> Look at them shake uncontrollably,
> like a woman writhing in childbirth.
> <a name="19:48:7">48:7</a> With an east wind
> you shatter the large ships.
> <a name="19:48:8">48:8</a> We heard about God’s mighty deeds, now we have seen them,
> in the city of the Lord, the invincible Warrior,
> in the city of our God.
> God makes it permanently secure. (Selah)
> <a name="19:48:9">48:9</a> We reflect on your loyal love, O God,
> within your temple.
> <a name="19:48:10">48:10</a> The praise you receive as far away as the ends of the earth
> is worthy of your reputation, O God.
> You execute justice!
> <a name="19:48:11">48:11</a> Mount Zion rejoices;
> the towns of Judah are happy,
> because of your acts of judgment.
> <a name="19:48:12">48:12</a> Walk around Zion! Encircle it!
> Count its towers!
> <a name="19:48:13">48:13</a> Consider its defenses!
> Walk through its fortresses,
> so you can tell the next generation about it!
> <a name="19:48:14">48:14</a> For God, our God, is our defender forever!
> He guides us!

### Psalm 49

For the music director, a psalm by the Korahites.

> <a name="19:49:1">49:1</a> Listen to this, all you nations!
> Pay attention, all you inhabitants of the world!
> <a name="19:49:2">49:2</a> Pay attention, all you people,
> both rich and poor!
> <a name="19:49:3">49:3</a> I will declare a wise saying;
> I will share my profound thoughts.
> <a name="19:49:4">49:4</a> I will learn a song that imparts wisdom;
> I will then sing my insightful song to the accompaniment of a harp.
> <a name="19:49:5">49:5</a> Why should I be afraid in times of trouble,
> when the sinful deeds of deceptive men threaten to overwhelm me?
> <a name="19:49:6">49:6</a> They trust in their wealth
> and boast in their great riches.
> <a name="19:49:7">49:7</a> Certainly a man cannot rescue his brother;
> he cannot pay God an adequate ransom price
> <a name="19:49:8">49:8</a> (the ransom price for a human life is too high,
> and people go to their final destiny),
> <a name="19:49:9">49:9</a> so that he might continue to live forever
> and not experience death.
> <a name="19:49:10">49:10</a> Surely one sees that even wise people die;
> fools and spiritually insensitive people all pass away
> and leave their wealth to others.
> <a name="19:49:11">49:11</a> Their grave becomes their permanent residence,
> their eternal dwelling place.
> They name their lands after themselves,
> <a name="19:49:12">49:12</a> but, despite their wealth, people do not last,
> they are like animals that perish.
> <a name="19:49:13">49:13</a> This is the destiny of fools,
> and of those who approve of their philosophy. (Selah)
> <a name="19:49:14">49:14</a> They will travel to Sheol like sheep,
> with death as their shepherd.
> The godly will rule over them when the day of vindication dawns;
> Sheol will consume their bodies and they will no longer live in impressive houses.
> <a name="19:49:15">49:15</a> But God will rescue my life from the power of Sheol;
> certainly he will pull me to safety. (Selah)
> <a name="19:49:16">49:16</a> Do not be afraid when a man becomes rich
> and his wealth multiplies!
> <a name="19:49:17">49:17</a> For he will take nothing with him when he dies;
> his wealth will not follow him down into the grave.
> <a name="19:49:18">49:18</a> He pronounces this blessing on himself while he is alive:
> “May men praise you, for you have done well!”
> <a name="19:49:19">49:19</a> But he will join his ancestors;
> they will never again see the light of day.
> <a name="19:49:20">49:20</a> Wealthy people do not understand;
> they are like animals that perish.

### Psalm 50

A psalm by Asaph.

> <a name="19:50:1">50:1</a> El, God, the Lord speaks,
> and summons the earth to come from the east and west.
> <a name="19:50:2">50:2</a> From Zion, the most beautiful of all places,
> God comes in splendor.
> <a name="19:50:3">50:3</a> Our God approaches and is not silent;
> consuming fire goes ahead of him
> and all around him a storm rages.
> <a name="19:50:4">50:4</a> He summons the heavens above,
> as well as the earth, so that he might judge his people.
> <a name="19:50:5">50:5</a> He says:
> “Assemble my covenant people before me,
> those who ratified a covenant with me by sacrifice!”
> <a name="19:50:6">50:6</a> The heavens declare his fairness,
> for God is judge. (Selah)
> <a name="19:50:7">50:7</a> He says:
> “Listen my people! I am speaking!
> Listen Israel! I am accusing you!
> I am God, your God!
> <a name="19:50:8">50:8</a> I am not condemning you because of your sacrifices,
> or because of your burnt sacrifices that you continually offer me.
> <a name="19:50:9">50:9</a> I do not need to take a bull from your household
> or goats from your sheepfolds.
> <a name="19:50:10">50:10</a> For every wild animal in the forest belongs to me,
> as well as the cattle that graze on a thousand hills.
> <a name="19:50:11">50:11</a> I keep track of every bird in the hills,
> and the insects of the field are mine.
> <a name="19:50:12">50:12</a> Even if I were hungry, I would not tell you,
> for the world and all it contains belong to me.
> <a name="19:50:13">50:13</a> Do I eat the flesh of bulls?
> Do I drink the blood of goats?
> <a name="19:50:14">50:14</a> Present to God a thank-offering!
> Repay your vows to the Sovereign One!
> <a name="19:50:15">50:15</a> Pray to me when you are in trouble!
> I will deliver you and vindicate you!”
> <a name="19:50:16">50:16</a> God says this to the evildoer:
> “How can you declare my commands,
> and talk about my covenant?
> <a name="19:50:17">50:17</a> For you hate instruction
> and reject my words.
> <a name="19:50:18">50:18</a> When you see a thief, you join him;
> you associate with men who are unfaithful to their wives.
> <a name="19:50:19">50:19</a> You do damage with words,
> and use your tongue to deceive.
> <a name="19:50:20">50:20</a> You plot against your brother;
> you slander your own brother.
> <a name="19:50:21">50:21</a> When you did these things, I was silent,
> so you thought I was exactly like you.
> But now I will condemn you
> and state my case against you!
> <a name="19:50:22">50:22</a> Carefully consider this, you who reject God!
> Otherwise I will rip you to shreds
> and no one will be able to rescue you.
> <a name="19:50:23">50:23</a> Whoever presents a thank-offering honors me.
> To whoever obeys my commands, I will reveal my power to deliver.”

### Psalm 51

For the music director; a psalm of David, written when Nathan the prophet confronted him after David’s affair with Bathsheba.

> <a name="19:51:1">51:1</a> Have mercy on me, O God, because of your loyal love!
> Because of your great compassion, wipe away my rebellious acts!
> <a name="19:51:2">51:2</a> Scrub away my wrongdoing!
> Cleanse me of my sin!
> <a name="19:51:3">51:3</a> For I am aware of my rebellious acts;
> I am forever conscious of my sin.
> <a name="19:51:4">51:4</a> Against you, especially you, I have sinned;
> I have done what is sinful in your sight.
> So you are just when you confront me;
> you are right when you condemn me.
> <a name="19:51:5">51:5</a> Look, I was prone to do wrong from birth;
> I was a sinner the moment my mother conceived me.
> <a name="19:51:6">51:6</a> Look, you desire integrity in the inner man;
> you want me to possess wisdom.
> <a name="19:51:7">51:7</a> Sprinkle me with water and I will be pure;
> wash me and I will be whiter than snow.
> <a name="19:51:8">51:8</a> Give me the ecstatic joy of being forgiven!
> May the bones you crushed rejoice!
> <a name="19:51:9">51:9</a> Hide your face from my sins!
> Wipe away all my wrong acts!
> <a name="19:51:10">51:10</a> Create for me a pure heart!
> Transform me and give me integrity!
> <a name="19:51:11">51:11</a> Do not reject me!
> Do not take your Holy Spirit away from me!
> <a name="19:51:12">51:12</a> Let me again experience the joy of your deliverance!
> Sustain me by giving me the desire to obey!
> <a name="19:51:13">51:13</a> Then I will teach rebels your merciful ways,
> and sinners will turn to you.
> <a name="19:51:14">51:14</a> Rescue me from the guilt of murder, O God, the God who delivers me!
> Then my tongue will shout for joy because of your deliverance.
> <a name="19:51:15">51:15</a> O sovereign Master, give me reason to celebrate!
> Then my mouth will praise you.
> <a name="19:51:16">51:16</a> Certainly you do not want a sacrifice, or else I would offer it;
> you do not desire a burnt sacrifice.
> <a name="19:51:17">51:17</a> The “sacrifices” God desires are a humble attitude—
> O God, a humble and repentant heart you will not reject.
> <a name="19:51:18">51:18</a> Be favorably disposed to Zion!
> Build the walls of Jerusalem!
> <a name="19:51:19">51:19</a> Then you will accept the proper sacrifices, burnt sacrifices and whole offerings;
> then bulls will be sacrificed on your altar.

### Psalm 52

For the music director; a well-written song by David. It was written when Doeg the Edomite went and informed Saul: “David has arrived at the home of Ahimelech.”

> <a name="19:52:1">52:1</a> Why do you boast about your evil plans, O powerful man?
> God’s loyal love protects me all day long!
> <a name="19:52:2">52:2</a> Your tongue carries out your destructive plans;
> it is as effective as a sharp razor, O deceiver.
> <a name="19:52:3">52:3</a> You love evil more than good,
> lies more than speaking the truth. (Selah)
> <a name="19:52:4">52:4</a> You love to use all the words that destroy,
> and the tongue that deceives.
> <a name="19:52:5">52:5</a> Yet God will make you a permanent heap of ruins.
> He will scoop you up and remove you from your home;
> he will uproot you from the land of the living. (Selah)
> <a name="19:52:6">52:6</a> When the godly see this, they will be filled with awe,
> and will mock the evildoer, saying:
> <a name="19:52:7">52:7</a> “Look, here is the man who would not make God his protector!
> He trusted in his great wealth
> and was confident about his plans to destroy others.”
> <a name="19:52:8">52:8</a> But I am like a flourishing olive tree in the house of God;
> I continually trust in God’s loyal love.
> <a name="19:52:9">52:9</a> I will continually thank you when you execute judgment;
> I will rely on you, for your loyal followers know you are good.

### Psalm 53

For the music director; according to the machalath style; a well-written song by David.

> <a name="19:53:1">53:1</a> Fools say to themselves, “There is no God.”
> They sin and commit evil deeds;
> none of them does what is right.
> <a name="19:53:2">53:2</a> God looks down from heaven at the human race,
> to see if there is anyone who is wise and seeks God.
> <a name="19:53:3">53:3</a> Everyone rejects God;
> they are all morally corrupt.
> None of them does what is right,
> not even one!
> <a name="19:53:4">53:4</a> All those who behave wickedly do not understand—
> those who devour my people as if they were eating bread,
> and do not call out to God.
> <a name="19:53:5">53:5</a> They are absolutely terrified,
> even by things that do not normally cause fear.
> For God annihilates those who attack you.
> You are able to humiliate them because God has rejected them.
> <a name="19:53:6">53:6</a> I wish the deliverance of Israel would come from Zion!
> When God restores the well-being of his people,
> may Jacob rejoice,
> may Israel be happy!

### Psalm 54

For the music director, to be accompanied by stringed instruments; a well-written song by David. It was written when the Ziphites came and informed Saul: “David is hiding with us.”

> <a name="19:54:1">54:1</a> O God, deliver me by your name!
> Vindicate me by your power!
> <a name="19:54:2">54:2</a> O God, listen to my prayer!
> Pay attention to what I say!
> <a name="19:54:3">54:3</a> For foreigners attack me;
> ruthless men, who do not respect God, seek my life. (Selah)
> <a name="19:54:4">54:4</a> Look, God is my deliverer!
> The sovereign Master is among those who support me.
> <a name="19:54:5">54:5</a> May those who wait to ambush me be repaid for their evil!
> As a demonstration of your faithfulness, destroy them!
> <a name="19:54:6">54:6</a> With a freewill offering I will sacrifice to you!
> I will give thanks to your name, O Lord, for it is good!
> <a name="19:54:7">54:7</a> Surely he rescues me from all trouble,
> and I triumph over my enemies.

### Psalm 55

For the music director, to be accompanied by stringed instruments; a well-written song by David.

> <a name="19:55:1">55:1</a> Listen, O God, to my prayer!
> Do not ignore my appeal for mercy!
> <a name="19:55:2">55:2</a> Pay attention to me and answer me!
> I am so upset and distressed, I am beside myself,
> <a name="19:55:3">55:3</a> because of what the enemy says,
> and because of how the wicked pressure me,
> for they hurl trouble down upon me
> and angrily attack me.
> <a name="19:55:4">55:4</a> My heart beats violently within me;
> the horrors of death overcome me.
> <a name="19:55:5">55:5</a> Fear and panic overpower me;
> terror overwhelms me.
> <a name="19:55:6">55:6</a> I say, “I wish I had wings like a dove!
> I would fly away and settle in a safe place!
> <a name="19:55:7">55:7</a> Look, I will escape to a distant place;
> I will stay in the wilderness. (Selah)
> <a name="19:55:8">55:8</a> I will hurry off to a place that is safe
> from the strong wind and the gale.”
> <a name="19:55:9">55:9</a> Confuse them, O sovereign Master!
> Frustrate their plans!
> For I see violence and conflict in the city.
> <a name="19:55:10">55:10</a> Day and night they walk around on its walls,
> while wickedness and destruction are within it.
> <a name="19:55:11">55:11</a> Disaster is within it;
> violence and deceit do not depart from its public square.
> <a name="19:55:12">55:12</a> Indeed, it is not an enemy who insults me,
> or else I could bear it;
> it is not one who hates me who arrogantly taunts me,
> or else I could hide from him.
> <a name="19:55:13">55:13</a> But it is you, a man like me,
> my close friend in whom I confided.
> <a name="19:55:14">55:14</a> We would share personal thoughts with each other;
> in God’s temple we would walk together among the crowd.
> <a name="19:55:15">55:15</a> May death destroy them!
> May they go down alive into Sheol!
> For evil is in their dwelling place and in their midst.
> <a name="19:55:16">55:16</a> As for me, I will call out to God,
> and the Lord will deliver me.
> <a name="19:55:17">55:17</a> During the evening, morning, and noontime
> I will lament and moan,
> and he will hear me.
> <a name="19:55:18">55:18</a> He will rescue me and protect me from those who attack me,
> even though they greatly outnumber me.
> <a name="19:55:19">55:19</a> God, the one who has reigned as king from long ago,
> will hear and humiliate them. (Selah)
> They refuse to change,
> and do not fear God.
> <a name="19:55:20">55:20</a> He attacks his friends;
> he breaks his solemn promises to them.
> <a name="19:55:21">55:21</a> His words are as smooth as butter,
> but he harbors animosity in his heart.
> His words seem softer than oil,
> but they are really like sharp swords.
> <a name="19:55:22">55:22</a> Throw your burden upon the Lord,
> and he will sustain you.
> He will never allow the godly to be upended.
> <a name="19:55:23">55:23</a> But you, O God, will bring them down to the deep Pit.
> Violent and deceitful people will not live even half a normal lifespan.
> But as for me, I trust in you.

### Psalm 56

For the music director; according to the yonath-elem-rechovim style; a prayer of David, written when the Philistines captured him in Gath.

> <a name="19:56:1">56:1</a> Have mercy on me, O God, for men are attacking me!
> All day long hostile enemies are tormenting me.
> <a name="19:56:2">56:2</a> Those who anticipate my defeat attack me all day long.
> Indeed, many are fighting against me, O Exalted One.
> <a name="19:56:3">56:3</a> When I am afraid,
> I trust in you.
> <a name="19:56:4">56:4</a> In God—I boast in his promise—
> in God I trust, I am not afraid.
> What can mere men do to me?
> <a name="19:56:5">56:5</a> All day long they cause me trouble;
> they make a habit of plotting my demise.
> <a name="19:56:6">56:6</a> They stalk and lurk;
> they watch my every step,
> as they prepare to take my life.
> <a name="19:56:7">56:7</a> Because they are bent on violence, do not let them escape!
> In your anger bring down the nations, O God!
> <a name="19:56:8">56:8</a> You keep track of my misery.
> Put my tears in your leather container!
> Are they not recorded in your scroll?
> <a name="19:56:9">56:9</a> My enemies will turn back when I cry out to you for help;
> I know that God is on my side.
> <a name="19:56:10">56:10</a> In God—I boast in his promise—
> in the Lord—I boast in his promise—
> <a name="19:56:11">56:11</a> in God I trust, I am not afraid.
> What can mere men do to me?
> <a name="19:56:12">56:12</a> I am obligated to fulfill the vows I made to you, O God;
> I will give you the thank-offerings you deserve,
> <a name="19:56:13">56:13</a> when you deliver my life from death.
> You keep my feet from stumbling,
> so that I might serve God as I enjoy life.

### Psalm 57

For the music director; according to the al-tashcheth style; a prayer of David, written when he fled from Saul into the cave.

> <a name="19:57:1">57:1</a> Have mercy on me, O God! Have mercy on me!
> For in you I have taken shelter.
> In the shadow of your wings I take shelter
> until trouble passes.
> <a name="19:57:2">57:2</a> I cry out for help to the sovereign God,
> to the God who vindicates me.
> <a name="19:57:3">57:3</a> May he send help from heaven and deliver me
> from my enemies who hurl insults! (Selah)
> May God send his loyal love and faithfulness!
> <a name="19:57:4">57:4</a> I am surrounded by lions;
> I lie down among those who want to devour me;
> men whose teeth are spears and arrows,
> whose tongues are a sharp sword.
> <a name="19:57:5">57:5</a> Rise up above the sky, O God!
> May your splendor cover the whole earth!
> <a name="19:57:6">57:6</a> They have prepared a net to trap me;
> I am discouraged.
> They have dug a pit for me.
> They will fall into it! (Selah)
> <a name="19:57:7">57:7</a> I am determined, O God! I am determined!
> I will sing and praise you!
> <a name="19:57:8">57:8</a> Awake, my soul!
> Awake, O stringed instrument and harp!
> I will wake up at dawn!
> <a name="19:57:9">57:9</a> I will give you thanks before the nations, O Master!
> I will sing praises to you before foreigners!
> <a name="19:57:10">57:10</a> For your loyal love extends beyond the sky,
> and your faithfulness reaches the clouds.
> <a name="19:57:11">57:11</a> Rise up above the sky, O God!
> May your splendor cover the whole earth!

### Psalm 58

For the music director; according to the al-tashcheth style; a prayer of David.

> <a name="19:58:1">58:1</a> Do you rulers really pronounce just decisions?
> Do you judge people fairly?
> <a name="19:58:2">58:2</a> No! You plan how to do what is unjust;
> you deal out violence in the earth.
> <a name="19:58:3">58:3</a> The wicked turn aside from birth;
> liars go astray as soon as they are born.
> <a name="19:58:4">58:4</a> Their venom is like that of a snake,
> like a deaf serpent that does not hear,
> <a name="19:58:5">58:5</a> that does not respond to the magicians,
> or to a skilled snake-charmer.
> <a name="19:58:6">58:6</a> O God, break the teeth in their mouths!
> Smash the jawbones of the lions, O Lord!
> <a name="19:58:7">58:7</a> Let them disappear like water that flows away!
> Let them wither like grass!
> <a name="19:58:8">58:8</a> Let them be like a snail that melts away as it moves along!
> Let them be like stillborn babies that never see the sun!
> <a name="19:58:9">58:9</a> Before the kindling is even placed under your pots,
> he will sweep it away along with both the raw and cooked meat.
> <a name="19:58:10">58:10</a> The godly will rejoice when they see vengeance carried out;
> they will bathe their feet in the blood of the wicked.
> <a name="19:58:11">58:11</a> Then observers will say,
> “Yes indeed, the godly are rewarded!
> Yes indeed, there is a God who judges in the earth!”

### Psalm 59

For the music director; according to the al-tashcheth style; a prayer of David, written when Saul sent men to surround his house and murder him.

> <a name="19:59:1">59:1</a> Deliver me from my enemies, my God!
> Protect me from those who attack me!
> <a name="19:59:2">59:2</a> Deliver me from evildoers!
> Rescue me from violent men!
> <a name="19:59:3">59:3</a> For look, they wait to ambush me;
> powerful men stalk me,
> but not because I have rebelled or sinned, O Lord.
> <a name="19:59:4">59:4</a> Though I have done nothing wrong, they are anxious to attack.
> Spring into action and help me! Take notice of me!
> <a name="19:59:5">59:5</a> You, O Lord God, the invincible warrior, the God of Israel,
> rouse yourself and punish all the nations!
> Have no mercy on any treacherous evildoers! (Selah)
> <a name="19:59:6">59:6</a> They return in the evening;
> they growl like a dog
> and prowl around outside the city.
> <a name="19:59:7">59:7</a> Look, they hurl insults at me
> and openly threaten to kill me,
> for they say,
> “Who hears?”
> <a name="19:59:8">59:8</a> But you, O Lord, laugh in disgust at them;
> you taunt all the nations.
> <a name="19:59:9">59:9</a> You are my source of strength! I will wait for you!
> For God is my refuge.
> <a name="19:59:10">59:10</a> The God who loves me will help me;
> God will enable me to triumph over my enemies.
> <a name="19:59:11">59:11</a> Do not strike them dead suddenly,
> because then my people might forget the lesson.
> Use your power to make them homeless vagabonds and then bring them down,
> O sovereign Master who shields us!
> <a name="19:59:12">59:12</a> They speak sinful words.
> So let them be trapped by their own pride
> and by the curses and lies they speak!
> <a name="19:59:13">59:13</a> Angrily wipe them out! Wipe them out so they vanish!
> Let them know that God rules
> in Jacob and to the ends of the earth! (Selah)
> <a name="19:59:14">59:14</a> They return in the evening;
> they growl like a dog
> and prowl around outside the city.
> <a name="19:59:15">59:15</a> They wander around looking for something to eat;
> they refuse to sleep until they are full.
> <a name="19:59:16">59:16</a> As for me, I will sing about your strength;
> I will praise your loyal love in the morning.
> For you are my refuge
> and my place of shelter when I face trouble.
> <a name="19:59:17">59:17</a> You are my source of strength! I will sing praises to you!
> For God is my refuge, the God who loves me.

### Psalm 60

For the music director; according to the shushan-eduth style; a prayer of David written to instruct others. It was written when he fought against Aram Naharaim and Aram-Zobah. That was when Joab turned back and struck down 12,000 Edomites in the Valley of Salt.

> <a name="19:60:1">60:1</a> O God, you have rejected us.
> You suddenly turned on us in your anger.
> Please restore us!
> <a name="19:60:2">60:2</a> You made the earth quake; you split it open.
> Repair its breaches, for it is ready to fall.
> <a name="19:60:3">60:3</a> You have made your people experience hard times;
> you have made us drink intoxicating wine.
> <a name="19:60:4">60:4</a> You have given your loyal followers a rallying flag,
> so that they might seek safety from the bow. (Selah)
> <a name="19:60:5">60:5</a> Deliver by your power and answer me,
> so that the ones you love may be safe.
> <a name="19:60:6">60:6</a> God has spoken in his sanctuary:
> “I will triumph! I will parcel out Shechem;
> the Valley of Succoth I will measure off.
> <a name="19:60:7">60:7</a> Gilead belongs to me,
> as does Manasseh!
> Ephraim is my helmet,
> Judah my royal scepter.
> <a name="19:60:8">60:8</a> Moab is my washbasin.
> I will make Edom serve me.
> I will shout in triumph over Philistia.”
> <a name="19:60:9">60:9</a> Who will lead me into the fortified city?
> Who will bring me to Edom?
> <a name="19:60:10">60:10</a> Have you not rejected us, O God?
> O God, you do not go into battle with our armies.
> <a name="19:60:11">60:11</a> Give us help against the enemy,
> for any help men might offer is futile.
> <a name="19:60:12">60:12</a> By God’s power we will conquer;
> he will trample down our enemies.

### Psalm 61

For the music director; to be played on a stringed instrument; written by David.

> <a name="19:61:1">61:1</a> O God, hear my cry for help!
> Pay attention to my prayer!
> <a name="19:61:2">61:2</a> From the most remote place on earth
> I call out to you in my despair.
> Lead me up to an inaccessible rocky summit!
> <a name="19:61:3">61:3</a> Indeed, you are my shelter,
> a strong tower that protects me from the enemy.
> <a name="19:61:4">61:4</a> I will be a permanent guest in your home;
> I will find shelter in the protection of your wings. (Selah)
> <a name="19:61:5">61:5</a> For you, O God, hear my vows;
> you grant me the reward that belongs to your loyal followers.
> <a name="19:61:6">61:6</a> Give the king long life!
> Make his lifetime span several generations!
> <a name="19:61:7">61:7</a> May he reign forever before God!
> Decree that your loyal love and faithfulness should protect him.
> <a name="19:61:8">61:8</a> Then I will sing praises to your name continually,
> as I fulfill my vows day after day.

### Psalm 62

For the music director, Jeduthun; a psalm of David.

> <a name="19:62:1">62:1</a> For God alone I patiently wait;
> he is the one who delivers me.
> <a name="19:62:2">62:2</a> He alone is my protector and deliverer.
> He is my refuge; I will not be upended.
> <a name="19:62:3">62:3</a> How long will you threaten a man?
> All of you are murderers,
> as dangerous as a leaning wall or an unstable fence.
> <a name="19:62:4">62:4</a> They spend all their time planning how to bring him down.
> They love to use deceit;
> they pronounce blessings with their mouths,
> but inwardly they utter curses. (Selah)
> <a name="19:62:5">62:5</a> Patiently wait for God alone, my soul!
> For he is the one who gives me confidence.
> <a name="19:62:6">62:6</a> He alone is my protector and deliverer.
> He is my refuge; I will not be upended.
> <a name="19:62:7">62:7</a> God delivers me and exalts me;
> God is my strong protector and my shelter.
> <a name="19:62:8">62:8</a> Trust in him at all times, you people!
> Pour out your hearts before him!
> God is our shelter! (Selah)
> <a name="19:62:9">62:9</a> Men are nothing but a mere breath;
> human beings are unreliable.
> When they are weighed in the scales,
> all of them together are lighter than air.
> <a name="19:62:10">62:10</a> Do not trust in what you can gain by oppression!
> Do not put false confidence in what you can gain by robbery!
> If wealth increases, do not become attached to it!
> <a name="19:62:11">62:11</a> God has declared one principle;
> two principles I have heard:
> God is strong,
> <a name="19:62:12">62:12</a> and you, O sovereign Master, demonstrate loyal love.
> For you repay men for what they do.

### Psalm 63

A psalm of David, written when he was in the Judean wilderness.

> <a name="19:63:1">63:1</a> O God, you are my God! I long for you!
> My soul thirsts for you,
> my flesh yearns for you,
> in a dry and parched land where there is no water.
> <a name="19:63:2">63:2</a> Yes, in the sanctuary I have seen you,
> and witnessed your power and splendor.
> <a name="19:63:3">63:3</a> Because experiencing your loyal love is better than life itself,
> my lips will praise you.
> <a name="19:63:4">63:4</a> For this reason I will praise you while I live;
> in your name I will lift up my hands.
> <a name="19:63:5">63:5</a> As if with choice meat you satisfy my soul.
> My mouth joyfully praises you,
> <a name="19:63:6">63:6</a> whenever I remember you on my bed,
> and think about you during the nighttime hours.
> <a name="19:63:7">63:7</a> For you are my deliverer;
> under your wings I rejoice.
> <a name="19:63:8">63:8</a> My soul pursues you;
> your right hand upholds me.
> <a name="19:63:9">63:9</a> Enemies seek to destroy my life,
> but they will descend into the depths of the earth.
> <a name="19:63:10">63:10</a> Each one will be handed over to the sword;
> their corpses will be eaten by jackals.
> <a name="19:63:11">63:11</a> But the king will rejoice in God;
> everyone who takes oaths in his name will boast,
> for the mouths of those who speak lies will be shut up.

### Psalm 64

For the music director; a psalm of David.

> <a name="19:64:1">64:1</a> Listen to me, O God, as I offer my lament!
> Protect my life from the enemy’s terrifying attacks.
> <a name="19:64:2">64:2</a> Hide me from the plots of evil men,
> from the crowd of evildoers.
> <a name="19:64:3">64:3</a> They sharpen their tongues like a sword;
> they aim their arrow, a slanderous charge,
> <a name="19:64:4">64:4</a> in order to shoot down the innocent in secluded places.
> They shoot at him suddenly and are unafraid of retaliation.
> <a name="19:64:5">64:5</a> They encourage one another to carry out their evil deed.
> They plan how to hide snares,
> and boast, “Who will see them?”
> <a name="19:64:6">64:6</a> They devise unjust schemes;
> they disguise a well-conceived plot.
> Man’s inner thoughts cannot be discovered.
> <a name="19:64:7">64:7</a> But God will shoot at them;
> suddenly they will be wounded by an arrow.
> <a name="19:64:8">64:8</a> Their slander will bring about their demise.
> All who see them will shudder,
> <a name="19:64:9">64:9</a> and all people will fear.
> They will proclaim what God has done,
> and reflect on his deeds.
> <a name="19:64:10">64:10</a> The godly will rejoice in the Lord
> and take shelter in him.
> All the morally upright will boast.

### Psalm 65

For the music director; a psalm of David, a song.

> <a name="19:65:1">65:1</a> Praise awaits you, O God, in Zion.
> Vows made to you are fulfilled.
> <a name="19:65:2">65:2</a> You hear prayers;
> all people approach you.
> <a name="19:65:3">65:3</a> Our record of sins overwhelms me,
> but you forgive our acts of rebellion.
> <a name="19:65:4">65:4</a> How happy is the one whom you choose,
> and allow to live in your palace courts.
> May we be satisfied with the good things of your house—
> your holy palace.
> <a name="19:65:5">65:5</a> You answer our prayers by performing awesome acts of deliverance,
> O God, our savior.
> All the ends of the earth trust in you,
> as well as those living across the wide seas.
> <a name="19:65:6">65:6</a> You created the mountains by your power,
> and demonstrated your strength.
> <a name="19:65:7">65:7</a> You calm the raging seas
> and their roaring waves,
> as well as the commotion made by the nations.
> <a name="19:65:8">65:8</a> Even those living in the most remote areas are awestruck by your acts;
> you cause those living in the east and west to praise you.
> <a name="19:65:9">65:9</a> You visit the earth and give it rain;
> you make it rich and fertile
> with overflowing streams full of water.
> You provide grain for them,
> for you prepare the earth to yield its crops.
> <a name="19:65:10">65:10</a> You saturate its furrows,
> and soak its plowed ground.
> With rain showers you soften its soil,
> and make its crops grow.
> <a name="19:65:11">65:11</a> You crown the year with your good blessings,
> and you leave abundance in your wake.
> <a name="19:65:12">65:12</a> The pastures in the wilderness glisten with moisture,
> and the hills are clothed with joy.
> <a name="19:65:13">65:13</a> The meadows are clothed with sheep,
> and the valleys are covered with grain.
> They shout joyfully, yes, they sing.

### Psalm 66

For the music director; a song, a psalm.

> <a name="19:66:1">66:1</a> Shout out praise to God, all the earth!
> <a name="19:66:2">66:2</a> Sing praises about the majesty of his reputation!
> Give him the honor he deserves!
> <a name="19:66:3">66:3</a> Say to God:
> “How awesome are your deeds!
> Because of your great power your enemies cower in fear before you.
> <a name="19:66:4">66:4</a> All the earth worships you
> and sings praises to you!
> They sing praises to your name!” (Selah)
> <a name="19:66:5">66:5</a> Come and witness God’s exploits!
> His acts on behalf of people are awesome!
> <a name="19:66:6">66:6</a> He turned the sea into dry land;
> they passed through the river on foot.
> Let us rejoice in him there!
> <a name="19:66:7">66:7</a> He rules by his power forever;
> he watches the nations.
> Stubborn rebels should not exalt themselves. (Selah)
> <a name="19:66:8">66:8</a> Praise our God, you nations!
> Loudly proclaim his praise!
> <a name="19:66:9">66:9</a> He preserves our lives
> and does not allow our feet to slip.
> <a name="19:66:10">66:10</a> For you, O God, tested us;
> you purified us like refined silver.
> <a name="19:66:11">66:11</a> You led us into a trap;
> you caused us to suffer.
> <a name="19:66:12">66:12</a> You allowed men to ride over our heads;
> we passed through fire and water,
> but you brought us out into a wide open place.
> <a name="19:66:13">66:13</a> I will enter your temple with burnt sacrifices;
> I will fulfill the vows I made to you,
> <a name="19:66:14">66:14</a> which my lips uttered
> and my mouth spoke when I was in trouble.
> <a name="19:66:15">66:15</a> I will offer up to you fattened animals as burnt sacrifices,
> along with the smell of sacrificial rams.
> I will offer cattle and goats. (Selah)
> <a name="19:66:16">66:16</a> Come! Listen, all you who are loyal to God!
> I will declare what he has done for me.
> <a name="19:66:17">66:17</a> I cried out to him for help
> and praised him with my tongue.
> <a name="19:66:18">66:18</a> If I had harbored sin in my heart,
> the sovereign Master would not have listened.
> <a name="19:66:19">66:19</a> However, God heard;
> he listened to my prayer.
> <a name="19:66:20">66:20</a> God deserves praise,
> for he did not reject my prayer
> or abandon his love for me!

### Psalm 67

For the music director; to be accompanied by stringed instruments; a psalm, a song.

> <a name="19:67:1">67:1</a> May God show us his favor and bless us!
> May he smile on us! (Selah)
> <a name="19:67:2">67:2</a> Then those living on earth will know what you are like;
> all nations will know how you deliver your people.
> <a name="19:67:3">67:3</a> Let the nations thank you, O God!
> Let all the nations thank you!
> <a name="19:67:4">67:4</a> Let foreigners rejoice and celebrate!
> For you execute justice among the nations,
> and govern the people living on earth. (Selah)
> <a name="19:67:5">67:5</a> Let the nations thank you, O God!
> Let all the nations thank you!
> <a name="19:67:6">67:6</a> The earth yields its crops.
> May God, our God, bless us!
> <a name="19:67:7">67:7</a> May God bless us!
> Then all the ends of the earth will give him the honor he deserves.

### Psalm 68

For the music director; by David, a psalm, a song.

> <a name="19:68:1">68:1</a> God springs into action!
> His enemies scatter;
> his adversaries run from him.
> <a name="19:68:2">68:2</a> As smoke is driven away by the wind, so you drive them away.
> As wax melts before fire,
> so the wicked are destroyed before God.
> <a name="19:68:3">68:3</a> But the godly are happy;
> they rejoice before God
> and are overcome with joy.
> <a name="19:68:4">68:4</a> Sing to God! Sing praises to his name!
> Exalt the one who rides on the clouds!
> For the Lord is his name!
> Rejoice before him!
> <a name="19:68:5">68:5</a> He is a father to the fatherless
> and an advocate for widows.
> God rules from his holy palace.
> <a name="19:68:6">68:6</a> God settles those who have been deserted in their own homes;
> he frees prisoners and grants them prosperity.
> But sinful rebels live in the desert.
> <a name="19:68:7">68:7</a> O God, when you lead your people into battle,
> when you march through the desert, (Selah)
> <a name="19:68:8">68:8</a> the earth shakes,
> yes, the heavens pour down rain
> before God, the God of Sinai,
> before God, the God of Israel.
> <a name="19:68:9">68:9</a> O God, you cause abundant showers to fall on your chosen people.
> When they are tired, you sustain them,
> <a name="19:68:10">68:10</a> for you live among them.
> You sustain the oppressed with your good blessings, O God.
> <a name="19:68:11">68:11</a> The sovereign Master speaks;
> many, many women spread the good news.
> <a name="19:68:12">68:12</a> Kings leading armies run away—they run away!
> The lovely lady of the house divides up the loot.
> <a name="19:68:13">68:13</a> When you lie down among the sheepfolds,
> the wings of the dove are covered with silver
> and with glittering gold.
> <a name="19:68:14">68:14</a> When the sovereign judge scatters kings,
> let it snow on Zalmon!
> <a name="19:68:15">68:15</a> The mountain of Bashan is a towering mountain;
> the mountain of Bashan is a mountain with many peaks.
> <a name="19:68:16">68:16</a> Why do you look with envy, O mountains with many peaks,
> at the mountain where God has decided to live?
> Indeed the Lord will live there permanently!
> <a name="19:68:17">68:17</a> God has countless chariots;
> they number in the thousands.
> The sovereign Master comes from Sinai in holy splendor.
> <a name="19:68:18">68:18</a> You ascend on high,
> you have taken many captives.
> You receive tribute from men,
> including even sinful rebels.
> Indeed the Lord God lives there!
> <a name="19:68:19">68:19</a> The sovereign Master deserves praise!
> Day after day he carries our burden,
> the God who delivers us. (Selah)
> <a name="19:68:20">68:20</a> Our God is a God who delivers;
> the Lord, the sovereign Master, can rescue from death.
> <a name="19:68:21">68:21</a> Indeed God strikes the heads of his enemies,
> the hairy foreheads of those who persist in rebellion.
> <a name="19:68:22">68:22</a> The sovereign Master says,
> “I will retrieve them from Bashan,
> I will bring them back from the depths of the sea,
> <a name="19:68:23">68:23</a> so that your feet may stomp in their blood,
> and your dogs may eat their portion of the enemies’ corpses.”
> <a name="19:68:24">68:24</a> They see your processions, O God—
> the processions of my God, my king, who marches along in holy splendor.
> <a name="19:68:25">68:25</a> Singers walk in front;
> musicians follow playing their stringed instruments,
> in the midst of young women playing tambourines.
> <a name="19:68:26">68:26</a> In your large assemblies praise God,
> the sovereign Master, in the assemblies of Israel!
> <a name="19:68:27">68:27</a> There is little Benjamin, their ruler,
> and the princes of Judah in their robes,
> along with the princes of Zebulun and the princes of Naphtali.
> <a name="19:68:28">68:28</a> God has decreed that you will be powerful.
> O God, you who have acted on our behalf, demonstrate your power,
> <a name="19:68:29">68:29</a> as you come out of your temple in Jerusalem!
> Kings bring tribute to you.
> <a name="19:68:30">68:30</a> Sound your battle cry against the wild beast of the reeds,
> and the nations that assemble like a herd of calves led by bulls!
> They humble themselves and offer gold and silver as tribute.
> God scatters the nations that like to do battle.
> <a name="19:68:31">68:31</a> They come with red cloth from Egypt,
> Ethiopia voluntarily offers tribute to God.
> <a name="19:68:32">68:32</a> O kingdoms of the earth, sing to God!
> Sing praises to the sovereign Master, (Selah)
> <a name="19:68:33">68:33</a> to the one who rides through the sky from ancient times!
> Look! He thunders loudly.
> <a name="19:68:34">68:34</a> Acknowledge God’s power,
> his sovereignty over Israel,
> and the power he reveals in the skies!
> <a name="19:68:35">68:35</a> You are awe-inspiring, O God, as you emerge from your holy temple!
> It is the God of Israel who gives the people power and strength.
> God deserves praise!

### Psalm 69

For the music director; according to the tune of “Lilies;” by David.

> <a name="19:69:1">69:1</a> Deliver me, O God,
> for the water has reached my neck.
> <a name="19:69:2">69:2</a> I sink into the deep mire
> where there is no solid ground;
> I am in deep water,
> and the current overpowers me.
> <a name="19:69:3">69:3</a> I am exhausted from shouting for help;
> my throat is sore;
> my eyes grow tired of looking for my God.
> <a name="19:69:4">69:4</a> Those who hate me without cause are more numerous than the hairs of my head.
> Those who want to destroy me and are my enemies for no reason outnumber me.
> They make me “pay back” what I did not steal!
> <a name="19:69:5">69:5</a> O God, you are aware of my foolish sins;
> my faults are not hidden from you.
> <a name="19:69:6">69:6</a> Let none who rely on you be embarrassed because of me,
> O sovereign Lord and king!
> Let none who seek you be ashamed because of me,
> O God of Israel!
> <a name="19:69:7">69:7</a> For I suffer humiliation for your sake
> and am thoroughly disgraced.
> <a name="19:69:8">69:8</a> My own brothers treat me like a stranger;
> they act as if I were a foreigner.
> <a name="19:69:9">69:9</a> Certainly devotion to your temple consumes me;
> I endure the insults of those who insult you.
> <a name="19:69:10">69:10</a> I weep and refrain from eating food,
> which causes others to insult me.
> <a name="19:69:11">69:11</a> I wear sackcloth
> and they ridicule me.
> <a name="19:69:12">69:12</a> Those who sit at the city gate talk about me;
> drunkards mock me in their songs.
> <a name="19:69:13">69:13</a> O Lord, may you hear my prayer and be favorably disposed to me!
> O God, because of your great loyal love, answer me;
> deliver me because of your faithfulness!
> <a name="19:69:14">69:14</a> Rescue me from the mud! Don’t let me sink!
> Deliver me from those who hate me,
> from the deep water!
> <a name="19:69:15">69:15</a> Don’t let the current overpower me!
> Don’t let the deep swallow me up!
> Don’t let the pit devour me!
> <a name="19:69:16">69:16</a> Answer me, O Lord, for your loyal love is what I need!
> Because of your great compassion, turn toward me!
> <a name="19:69:17">69:17</a> Do not ignore your servant,
> for I am in trouble! Answer me right away!
> <a name="19:69:18">69:18</a> Come near me and defend me!
> Because of my enemies, rescue me!
> <a name="19:69:19">69:19</a> You know how I am insulted, humiliated and disgraced;
> you can see all my enemies.
> <a name="19:69:20">69:20</a> Their insults are painful and make me lose heart;
> I look for sympathy, but receive none,
> for comforters, but find none.
> <a name="19:69:21">69:21</a> They put a poisonous herb into my food,
> and to quench my thirst they give me vinegar to drink.
> <a name="19:69:22">69:22</a> May their dining table become a trap before them!
> May it be a snare for that group of friends!
> <a name="19:69:23">69:23</a> May their eyes be blinded!
> Make them incapable of standing up!
> <a name="19:69:24">69:24</a> Pour out your judgment on them!
> May your raging anger overtake them!
> <a name="19:69:25">69:25</a> May their camp become desolate!
> May no one be left alive in their tents!
> <a name="19:69:26">69:26</a> For they harass the one whom you discipline;
> they spread the news about the suffering of those whom you punish.
> <a name="19:69:27">69:27</a> Hold them accountable for all their sins!
> Do not vindicate them!
> <a name="19:69:28">69:28</a> May their names be wiped out of the scroll listing the living!
> Do not let their names be listed with the godly!
> <a name="19:69:29">69:29</a> I am oppressed and suffering!
> O God, deliver and protect me!
> <a name="19:69:30">69:30</a> I will sing praises to God’s name!
> I will magnify him as I give him thanks!
> <a name="19:69:31">69:31</a> That will please the Lord more than an ox or a bull
> with horns and hooves.
> <a name="19:69:32">69:32</a> The oppressed look on—let them rejoice!
> You who seek God, may you be encouraged!
> <a name="19:69:33">69:33</a> For the Lord listens to the needy;
> he does not despise those whom he punishes.
> <a name="19:69:34">69:34</a> Let the heavens and the earth praise him,
> along with the seas and everything that swims in them!
> <a name="19:69:35">69:35</a> For God will deliver Zion
> and rebuild the cities of Judah,
> and his people will again live in them and possess Zion.
> <a name="19:69:36">69:36</a> The descendants of his servants will inherit it,
> and those who are loyal to him will live in it.

### Psalm 70

For the music director; by David; written to get God’s attention.

> <a name="19:70:1">70:1</a> O God, please be willing to rescue me!
> O Lord, hurry and help me!
> <a name="19:70:2">70:2</a> May those who are trying to take my life
> be embarrassed and ashamed!
> May those who want to harm me
> be turned back and ashamed!
> <a name="19:70:3">70:3</a> May those who say, “Aha! Aha!”
> be driven back and disgraced!
> <a name="19:70:4">70:4</a> May all those who seek you be happy and rejoice in you!
> May those who love to experience your deliverance say continually,
> “May God be praised!”
> <a name="19:70:5">70:5</a> I am oppressed and needy!
> O God, hurry to me!
> You are my helper and my deliverer!
> O Lord, do not delay!

### Psalm 71

> <a name="19:71:1">71:1</a> In you, O Lord, I have taken shelter!
> Never let me be humiliated!
> <a name="19:71:2">71:2</a> Vindicate me by rescuing me!
> Listen to me! Deliver me!
> <a name="19:71:3">71:3</a> Be my protector and refuge,
> a stronghold where I can be safe!
> For you are my high ridge and my stronghold.
> <a name="19:71:4">71:4</a> My God, rescue me from the power of the wicked,
> from the hand of the cruel oppressor!
> <a name="19:71:5">71:5</a> For you give me confidence, O sovereign Master;
> O Lord, I have trusted in you since I was young.
> <a name="19:71:6">71:6</a> I have leaned on you since birth;
> you pulled me from my mother’s womb.
> I praise you continually.
> <a name="19:71:7">71:7</a> Many are appalled when they see me,
> but you are my secure shelter.
> <a name="19:71:8">71:8</a> I praise you constantly
> and speak of your splendor all day long.
> <a name="19:71:9">71:9</a> Do not reject me in my old age!
> When my strength fails, do not abandon me!
> <a name="19:71:10">71:10</a> For my enemies talk about me;
> those waiting for a chance to kill me plot my demise.
> <a name="19:71:11">71:11</a> They say, “God has abandoned him.
> Run and seize him, for there is no one who will rescue him!”
> <a name="19:71:12">71:12</a> O God, do not remain far away from me!
> My God, hurry and help me!
> <a name="19:71:13">71:13</a> May my accusers be humiliated and defeated!
> May those who want to harm me be covered with scorn and disgrace!
> <a name="19:71:14">71:14</a> As for me, I will wait continually,
> and will continue to praise you.
> <a name="19:71:15">71:15</a> I will tell about your justice,
> and all day long proclaim your salvation,
> though I cannot fathom its full extent.
> <a name="19:71:16">71:16</a> I will come and tell about the mighty acts of the sovereign Lord.
> I will proclaim your justice—yours alone.
> <a name="19:71:17">71:17</a> O God, you have taught me since I was young,
> and I am still declaring your amazing deeds.
> <a name="19:71:18">71:18</a> Even when I am old and gray,
> O God, do not abandon me,
> until I tell the next generation about your strength,
> and those coming after me about your power.
> <a name="19:71:19">71:19</a> Your justice, O God, extends to the skies above;
> you have done great things.
> O God, who can compare to you?
> <a name="19:71:20">71:20</a> Though you have allowed me to experience much trouble and distress,
> revive me once again!
> Bring me up once again from the depths of the earth!
> <a name="19:71:21">71:21</a> Raise me to a position of great honor!
> Turn and comfort me!
> <a name="19:71:22">71:22</a> I will express my thanks to you with a stringed instrument,
> praising your faithfulness, O my God!
> I will sing praises to you accompanied by a harp,
> O sovereign king of Israel!
> <a name="19:71:23">71:23</a> My lips will shout for joy! Yes, I will sing your praises!
> I will praise you when you rescue me!
> <a name="19:71:24">71:24</a> All day long my tongue will also tell about your justice,
> for those who want to harm me will be embarrassed and ashamed.

### Psalm 72

For Solomon.

> <a name="19:72:1">72:1</a> O God, grant the king the ability to make just decisions!
> Grant the king’s son the ability to make fair decisions!
> <a name="19:72:2">72:2</a> Then he will judge your people fairly,
> and your oppressed ones equitably.
> <a name="19:72:3">72:3</a> The mountains will bring news of peace to the people,
> and the hills will announce justice.
> <a name="19:72:4">72:4</a> He will defend the oppressed among the people;
> he will deliver the children of the poor
> and crush the oppressor.
> <a name="19:72:5">72:5</a> People will fear you as long as the sun and moon remain in the sky,
> for generation after generation.
> <a name="19:72:6">72:6</a> He will descend like rain on the mown grass,
> like showers that drench the earth.
> <a name="19:72:7">72:7</a> During his days the godly will flourish;
> peace will prevail as long as the moon remains in the sky.
> <a name="19:72:8">72:8</a> May he rule from sea to sea,
> and from the Euphrates River to the ends of the earth!
> <a name="19:72:9">72:9</a> Before him the coastlands will bow down,
> and his enemies will lick the dust.
> <a name="19:72:10">72:10</a> The kings of Tarshish and the coastlands will offer gifts;
> the kings of Sheba and Seba will bring tribute.
> <a name="19:72:11">72:11</a> All kings will bow down to him;
> all nations will serve him.
> <a name="19:72:12">72:12</a> For he will rescue the needy when they cry out for help,
> and the oppressed who have no defender.
> <a name="19:72:13">72:13</a> He will take pity on the poor and needy;
> the lives of the needy he will save.
> <a name="19:72:14">72:14</a> From harm and violence he will defend them;
> he will value their lives.
> <a name="19:72:15">72:15</a> May he live! May they offer him gold from Sheba!
> May they continually pray for him!
> May they pronounce blessings on him all day long!
> <a name="19:72:16">72:16</a> May there be an abundance of grain in the earth;
> on the tops of the mountains may it sway!
> May its fruit trees flourish like the forests of Lebanon!
> May its crops be as abundant as the grass of the earth!
> <a name="19:72:17">72:17</a> May his fame endure!
> May his dynasty last as long as the sun remains in the sky!
> May they use his name when they formulate their blessings!
> May all nations consider him to be favored by God!
> <a name="19:72:18">72:18</a> The Lord God, the God of Israel, deserves praise!
> He alone accomplishes amazing things!
> <a name="19:72:19">72:19</a> His glorious name deserves praise forevermore!
> May his majestic splendor fill the whole earth!
> We agree! We agree!
> <a name="19:72:20">72:20</a> This collection of the prayers of David son of Jesse ends here.

## Book 3 (73–89)

### Psalm 73

A psalm by Asaph.

> <a name="19:73:1">73:1</a> Certainly God is good to Israel,
> and to those whose motives are pure!
> <a name="19:73:2">73:2</a> But as for me, my feet almost slipped;
> my feet almost slid out from under me.
> <a name="19:73:3">73:3</a> For I envied those who are proud,
> as I observed the prosperity of the wicked.
> <a name="19:73:4">73:4</a> For they suffer no pain;
> their bodies are strong and well-fed.
> <a name="19:73:5">73:5</a> They are immune to the trouble common to men;
> they do not suffer as other men do.
> <a name="19:73:6">73:6</a> Arrogance is their necklace,
> and violence their clothing.
> <a name="19:73:7">73:7</a> Their prosperity causes them to do wrong;
> their thoughts are sinful.
> <a name="19:73:8">73:8</a> They mock and say evil things;
> they proudly threaten violence.
> <a name="19:73:9">73:9</a> They speak as if they rule in heaven,
> and lay claim to the earth.
> <a name="19:73:10">73:10</a> Therefore they have more than enough food to eat,
> and even suck up the water of the sea.
> <a name="19:73:11">73:11</a> They say, “How does God know what we do?
> Is the sovereign one aware of what goes on?”
> <a name="19:73:12">73:12</a> Take a good look! This is what the wicked are like,
> those who always have it so easy and get richer and richer.
> <a name="19:73:13">73:13</a> I concluded, “Surely in vain I have kept my motives pure
> and maintained a pure lifestyle.
> <a name="19:73:14">73:14</a> I suffer all day long,
> and am punished every morning.”
> <a name="19:73:15">73:15</a> If I had publicized these thoughts,
> I would have betrayed your loyal followers.
> <a name="19:73:16">73:16</a> When I tried to make sense of this,
> it was troubling to me.
> <a name="19:73:17">73:17</a> Then I entered the precincts of God’s temple,
> and understood the destiny of the wicked.
> <a name="19:73:18">73:18</a> Surely you put them in slippery places;
> you bring them down to ruin.
> <a name="19:73:19">73:19</a> How desolate they become in a mere moment!
> Terrifying judgments make their demise complete!
> <a name="19:73:20">73:20</a> They are like a dream after one wakes up.
> O sovereign Master, when you awake you will despise them.
> <a name="19:73:21">73:21</a> Yes, my spirit was bitter,
> and my insides felt sharp pain.
> <a name="19:73:22">73:22</a> I was ignorant and lacked insight;
> I was as senseless as an animal before you.
> <a name="19:73:23">73:23</a> But I am continually with you;
> you hold my right hand.
> <a name="19:73:24">73:24</a> You guide me by your wise advice,
> and then you will lead me to a position of honor.
> <a name="19:73:25">73:25</a> Whom do I have in heaven but you?
> I desire no one but you on earth.
> <a name="19:73:26">73:26</a> My flesh and my heart may grow weak,
> but God always protects my heart and gives me stability.
> <a name="19:73:27">73:27</a> Yes, look! Those far from you die;
> you destroy everyone who is unfaithful to you.
> <a name="19:73:28">73:28</a> But as for me, God’s presence is all I need.
> I have made the sovereign Lord my shelter,
> as I declare all the things you have done.

### Psalm 74

A well-written song by Asaph.

> <a name="19:74:1">74:1</a> Why, O God, have you permanently rejected us?
> Why does your anger burn against the sheep of your pasture?
> <a name="19:74:2">74:2</a> Remember your people whom you acquired in ancient times,
> whom you rescued so they could be your very own nation,
> as well as Mount Zion, where you dwell!
> <a name="19:74:3">74:3</a> Hurry and look at the permanent ruins,
> and all the damage the enemy has done to the temple!
> <a name="19:74:4">74:4</a> Your enemies roar in the middle of your sanctuary;
> they set up their battle flags.
> <a name="19:74:5">74:5</a> They invade like lumberjacks
> swinging their axes in a thick forest.
> <a name="19:74:6">74:6</a> And now they are tearing down all its engravings
> with axes and crowbars.
> <a name="19:74:7">74:7</a> They set your sanctuary on fire;
> they desecrate your dwelling place by knocking it to the ground.
> <a name="19:74:8">74:8</a> They say to themselves,
> “We will oppress all of them.”
> They burn down all the places where people worship God in the land.
> <a name="19:74:9">74:9</a> We do not see any signs of God’s presence;
> there are no longer any prophets
> and we have no one to tell us how long this will last.
> <a name="19:74:10">74:10</a> How long, O God, will the adversary hurl insults?
> Will the enemy blaspheme your name forever?
> <a name="19:74:11">74:11</a> Why do you remain inactive?
> Intervene and destroy him!
> <a name="19:74:12">74:12</a> But God has been my king from ancient times,
> performing acts of deliverance on the earth.
> <a name="19:74:13">74:13</a> You destroyed the sea by your strength;
> you shattered the heads of the sea monster in the water.
> <a name="19:74:14">74:14</a> You crushed the heads of Leviathan;
> you fed him to the people who live along the coast.
> <a name="19:74:15">74:15</a> You broke open the spring and the stream;
> you dried up perpetually flowing rivers.
> <a name="19:74:16">74:16</a> You established the cycle of day and night;
> you put the moon and sun in place.
> <a name="19:74:17">74:17</a> You set up all the boundaries of the earth;
> you created the cycle of summer and winter.
> <a name="19:74:18">74:18</a> Remember how the enemy hurls insults, O Lord,
> and how a foolish nation blasphemes your name!
> <a name="19:74:19">74:19</a> Do not hand the life of your dove over to a wild animal!
> Do not continue to disregard the lives of your oppressed people!
> <a name="19:74:20">74:20</a> Remember your covenant promises,
> for the dark regions of the earth are full of places where violence rules.
> <a name="19:74:21">74:21</a> Do not let the afflicted be turned back in shame!
> Let the oppressed and poor praise your name!
> <a name="19:74:22">74:22</a> Rise up, O God! Defend your honor!
> Remember how fools insult you all day long!
> <a name="19:74:23">74:23</a> Do not disregard what your enemies say,
> or the unceasing shouts of those who defy you.

### Psalm 75

For the music director; according to the al-tashcheth style; a psalm of Asaph; a song.

> <a name="19:75:1">75:1</a> We give thanks to you, O God! We give thanks!
> You reveal your presence;
> people tell about your amazing deeds.
> <a name="19:75:2">75:2</a> God says,
> “At the appointed times,
> I judge fairly.
> <a name="19:75:3">75:3</a> When the earth and all its inhabitants dissolve in fear,
> I make its pillars secure.” (Selah)
> <a name="19:75:4">75:4</a> I say to the proud, “Do not be proud,”
> and to the wicked, “Do not be so confident of victory!
> <a name="19:75:5">75:5</a> Do not be so certain you have won!
> Do not speak with your head held so high!
> <a name="19:75:6">75:6</a> For victory does not come from the east or west,
> or from the wilderness.
> <a name="19:75:7">75:7</a> For God is the judge!
> He brings one down and exalts another.
> <a name="19:75:8">75:8</a> For the Lord holds in his hand a cup full
> of foaming wine mixed with spices,
> and pours it out.
> Surely all the wicked of the earth
> will slurp it up and drink it to its very last drop.”
> <a name="19:75:9">75:9</a> As for me, I will continually tell what you have done;
> I will sing praises to the God of Jacob!
> <a name="19:75:10">75:10</a> God says,
> “I will bring down all the power of the wicked;
> the godly will be victorious.”

### Psalm 76

For the music director; to be accompanied by stringed instruments; a psalm of Asaph, a song.

> <a name="19:76:1">76:1</a> God has revealed himself in Judah;
> in Israel his reputation is great.
> <a name="19:76:2">76:2</a> He lives in Salem;
> he dwells in Zion.
> <a name="19:76:3">76:3</a> There he shattered the arrows,
> the shield, the sword, and the rest of the weapons of war. (Selah)
> <a name="19:76:4">76:4</a> You shine brightly and reveal your majesty,
> as you descend from the hills where you killed your prey.
> <a name="19:76:5">76:5</a> The bravehearted were plundered;
> they “fell asleep.”
> All the warriors were helpless.
> <a name="19:76:6">76:6</a> At the sound of your battle cry, O God of Jacob,
> both rider and horse “fell asleep.”
> <a name="19:76:7">76:7</a> You are awesome! Yes, you!
> Who can withstand your intense anger?
> <a name="19:76:8">76:8</a> From heaven you announced what their punishment would be.
> The earth was afraid and silent
> <a name="19:76:9">76:9</a> when God arose to execute judgment,
> and to deliver all the oppressed of the earth. (Selah)
> <a name="19:76:10">76:10</a> Certainly your angry judgment upon men will bring you praise;
> you reveal your anger in full measure.
> <a name="19:76:11">76:11</a> Make vows to the Lord your God and repay them!
> Let all those who surround him bring tribute to the awesome one!
> <a name="19:76:12">76:12</a> He humbles princes;
> the kings of the earth regard him as awesome.

### Psalm 77

For the music director, Jeduthun; a psalm of Asaph.

> <a name="19:77:1">77:1</a> I will cry out to God and call for help!
> I will cry out to God and he will pay attention to me.
> <a name="19:77:2">77:2</a> In my time of trouble I sought the sovereign Master.
> I kept my hand raised in prayer throughout the night.
> I refused to be comforted.
> <a name="19:77:3">77:3</a> I said, “I will remember God while I groan;
> I will think about him while my strength leaves me.” (Selah)
> <a name="19:77:4">77:4</a> You held my eyelids open;
> I was troubled and could not speak.
> <a name="19:77:5">77:5</a> I thought about the days of old,
> about ancient times.
> <a name="19:77:6">77:6</a> I said, “During the night I will remember the song I once sang;
> I will think very carefully.”
> I tried to make sense of what was happening.
> <a name="19:77:7">77:7</a> I asked, “Will the sovereign Master reject me forever?
> Will he never again show me his favor?
> <a name="19:77:8">77:8</a> Has his loyal love disappeared forever?
> Has his promise failed forever?
> <a name="19:77:9">77:9</a> Has God forgotten to be merciful?
> Has his anger stifled his compassion?”
> <a name="19:77:10">77:10</a> Then I said, “I am sickened by the thought
> that the Sovereign One might become inactive.
> <a name="19:77:11">77:11</a> I will remember the works of the Lord.
> Yes, I will remember the amazing things you did long ago!
> <a name="19:77:12">77:12</a> I will think about all you have done;
> I will reflect upon your deeds!”
> <a name="19:77:13">77:13</a> O God, your deeds are extraordinary!
> What god can compare to our great God?
> <a name="19:77:14">77:14</a> You are the God who does amazing things;
> you have revealed your strength among the nations.
> <a name="19:77:15">77:15</a> You delivered your people by your strength—
> the children of Jacob and Joseph. (Selah)
> <a name="19:77:16">77:16</a> The waters saw you, O God,
> the waters saw you and trembled.
> Yes, the depths of the sea shook with fear.
> <a name="19:77:17">77:17</a> The clouds poured down rain;
> the skies thundered.
> Yes, your arrows flashed about.
> <a name="19:77:18">77:18</a> Your thunderous voice was heard in the wind;
> the lightning bolts lit up the world;
> the earth trembled and shook.
> <a name="19:77:19">77:19</a> You walked through the sea;
> you passed through the surging waters,
> but left no footprints.
> <a name="19:77:20">77:20</a> You led your people like a flock of sheep,
> by the hand of Moses and Aaron.

### Psalm 78

A well-written song by Asaph.

> <a name="19:78:1">78:1</a> Pay attention, my people, to my instruction!
> Listen to the words I speak!
> <a name="19:78:2">78:2</a> I will sing a song that imparts wisdom;
> I will make insightful observations about the past.
> <a name="19:78:3">78:3</a> What we have heard and learned—
> that which our ancestors have told us—
> <a name="19:78:4">78:4</a> we will not hide from their descendants.
> We will tell the next generation
> about the Lord’s praiseworthy acts,
> about his strength and the amazing things he has done.
> <a name="19:78:5">78:5</a> He established a rule in Jacob;
> he set up a law in Israel.
> He commanded our ancestors
> to make his deeds known to their descendants,
> <a name="19:78:6">78:6</a> so that the next generation, children yet to be born,
> might know about them.
> They will grow up and tell their descendants about them.
> <a name="19:78:7">78:7</a> Then they will place their confidence in God.
> They will not forget the works of God,
> and they will obey his commands.
> <a name="19:78:8">78:8</a> Then they will not be like their ancestors,
> who were a stubborn and rebellious generation,
> a generation that was not committed
> and faithful to God.
> <a name="19:78:9">78:9</a> The Ephraimites were armed with bows,
> but they retreated in the day of battle.
> <a name="19:78:10">78:10</a> They did not keep their covenant with God,
> and they refused to obey his law.
> <a name="19:78:11">78:11</a> They forgot what he had done,
> the amazing things he had shown them.
> <a name="19:78:12">78:12</a> He did amazing things in the sight of their ancestors,
> in the land of Egypt, in the region of Zoan.
> <a name="19:78:13">78:13</a> He divided the sea and led them across it;
> he made the water stand in a heap.
> <a name="19:78:14">78:14</a> He led them with a cloud by day,
> and with the light of a fire all night long.
> <a name="19:78:15">78:15</a> He broke open rocks in the wilderness,
> and gave them enough water to fill the depths of the sea.
> <a name="19:78:16">78:16</a> He caused streams to flow from the rock,
> and made the water flow like rivers.
> <a name="19:78:17">78:17</a> Yet they continued to sin against him,
> and rebelled against the Sovereign One in the desert.
> <a name="19:78:18">78:18</a> They willfully challenged God
> by asking for food to satisfy their appetite.
> <a name="19:78:19">78:19</a> They insulted God, saying,
> “Is God really able to give us food in the wilderness?
